  &lt;/tr&gt; 
 &lt;/tbody&gt; 
&lt;/table&gt; 
&lt;h4 id="required-parameters"&gt;Required parameters&lt;/h4&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;ACCOUNT_ID = &amp;lt;&amp;lt;0358134xxxxx&amp;gt;&amp;gt;&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;REGION = &amp;lt;&amp;gt;&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;DATASET_ID = &amp;lt;&amp;lt;30c1e26a-e02a-4f2a-ac48-xxa1xxxxx916&amp;gt;&amp;gt;&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;TOPIC_ID = &amp;lt;&amp;gt;&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;h2 id="step-1-get-target-dataset-id"&gt;Step 1: Get target dataset ID&lt;/h2&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;Open the Quick Sight console. In the left navigation panel, select &lt;strong&gt;Data&lt;/strong&gt;, then switch to the &lt;strong&gt;Datasets&lt;/strong&gt; tab. Select the dataset that you want to enrich. The dataset ID is the UUID at the end of your browser’s URL.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;Example:&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/f1f836cb4ea6efb2a0b1b99f41ad8b103eff4b59/2026/07/06/ML-21217-3.jpg" alt="Amazon Quick console dataset URL with the dataset ID at the end" width="800"&gt;&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;h2 id="step-2-get-the-source-legacy-topic-id"&gt;Step 2: Get the source legacy Topic ID&lt;/h2&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;Open the Quick Sight console. In the left navigation panel, select &lt;strong&gt;Data&lt;/strong&gt;, then switch to the &lt;strong&gt;Topics&lt;/strong&gt; tab. Select the source legacy Topic that you want to migrate from. The Topic ID is the string at the end of your browser’s URL.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;Example:&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/f1f836cb4ea6efb2a0b1b99f41ad8b103eff4b59/2026/07/06/ML-21217-4.jpg" alt="Amazon Quick console Topics URL with the legacy Topic ID at the end" width="800"&gt;&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;h2 id="step-3-python-code-to-enrich-a-dataset-with-information-from-a-legacy-topic"&gt;Step 3: Python code to enrich a dataset with information from a legacy Topic&lt;/h2&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;The following script connects to the Quick Sight APIs, retrieves your existing legacy Topic metadata and target dataset schema, then intelligently maps every piece of business context to its new home in the dataset’s &lt;code&gt;SemanticModelConfiguration&lt;/code&gt;. Column descriptions and synonyms become &lt;code&gt;ColumnProperties&lt;/code&gt;, calculated fields are injected as &lt;code&gt;CreateColumnsStep&lt;/code&gt; entries in your data prep pipeline, and named entities, filters, and custom instructions are consolidated into a structured &lt;code&gt;CustomInstructions&lt;/code&gt; text block. After the mapping is complete, it applies the enriched payload directly to your dataset through a SigV4-signed API call. Your dataset becomes fully self-describing in a single execution, with no manual UI work and no risk of transcription errors.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;Save the following script as &lt;code&gt;enrich_dataset.py&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;div class="hide-language"&gt; 
 &lt;pre&gt;&lt;code class="language-python"&gt;"""
enrich_dataset_local.py --- Enrich a Quick Sight dataset with Legacy Topic metadata.
Usage: python enrich_dataset_local.py &amp;lt;topic_id&amp;gt; &amp;lt;dataset_id&amp;gt; &amp;lt;aws_account_id&amp;gt; &amp;lt;aws_region&amp;gt;
NOTE: Uses raw SigV4 API call to bypass botocore validation (requires botocore &amp;gt;= 1.43.11).
"""
import json
import sys
import boto3
import botocore.session
from botocore.auth import SigV4Auth
from botocore.awsrequest import AWSRequest
import urllib3
http = urllib3.PoolManager()

def raw_update_data_set(aws_account_id, dataset_id, payload, region):
    """Call UpdateDataSet via raw SigV4 request, bypassing botocore validation."""
    session = botocore.session.get_session()
    credentials = session.get_credentials().get_frozen_credentials()
    url = f"https://quicksight.{region}.amazonaws.com/accounts/{aws_account_id}/data-sets/{dataset_id}"
    body = json.dumps(payload)
    headers = {"Content-Type": "application/json"}
    request = AWSRequest(method="PUT", url=url, data=body, headers=headers)
    SigV4Auth(credentials, "quicksight", region).add_auth(request)
    response = http.request("PUT", request.url, headers=dict(request.headers), body=request.body)
    response_body = json.loads(response.data.decode("utf-8"))
    if response.status &amp;gt;= 400:
        raise Exception(f"UpdateDataSet failed ({response.status}): {json.dumps(response_body, indent=2)}")
    return response_body

def enrich_dataset(topic_id, dataset_id, aws_account_id, aws_region):
    qs = boto3.client("quicksight", region_name=aws_region)
    print(f"\n{'='*60}")
    print(f"  Dataset Enrichment")
    print(f"{'='*60}")
    print(f"  Topic ID:   {topic_id}")
    print(f"  Dataset ID: {dataset_id}")
    print(f"  Account:    {aws_account_id}")
    print(f"  Region:     {aws_region}")
    print(f"{'='*60}\n")
    # --- Fetch inputs from Quick Sight APIs ---
    print("[1/5] Fetching dataset schema...")
    ds_response = qs.describe_data_set(AwsAccountId=aws_account_id, DataSetId=dataset_id)
    ds = ds_response["DataSet"]
    print(f"      Dataset: {ds['Name']}")
    print(f"      ARN: {ds['Arn']}")
    print("[2/5] Fetching topic metadata...")
    topic_response = qs.describe_topic(AwsAccountId=aws_account_id, TopicId=topic_id)
    topic_raw = topic_response
    print(f"      Topic: {topic_raw['Topic'].get('Name', topic_id)}")
    print(f"      Datasets in topic: {len(topic_raw['Topic']['DataSets'])}")
    # --- Match topic dataset by ARN ---
    target_arn = ds["Arn"]
    topic_datasets = topic_raw["Topic"]["DataSets"]
    topic = None
    for td in topic_datasets:
        if td.get("DatasetArn") == target_arn:
            topic = td
            break
    if topic is None:
        print(f"      WARNING: No topic dataset matched ARN {target_arn}. Falling back to index 0.")
        topic = topic_datasets[0]
    else:
        print(f"      Matched topic dataset by ARN ✓")
    custom_instructions_str = topic_raw.get("CustomInstructions", {}).get("CustomInstructionsString", "")
    # --- Extract dataset structure ---
    physical_table_map = ds["PhysicalTableMap"]
    import_mode = ds.get("ImportMode", "SPICE")
    uses_new_experience = "DataPrepConfiguration" in ds
    print(f"      Experience: {'NEW (DataPrepConfiguration)' if uses_new_experience else 'OLD (LogicalTableMap)'}")
    if uses_new_experience:
        data_prep = ds["DataPrepConfiguration"]
    else:
        logical_table_map = ds["LogicalTableMap"]
    ptable_key = list(physical_table_map.keys())[0]
    # Auto-detect source type
    source_entry = physical_table_map[ptable_key]
    if "RelationalTable" in source_entry:
        input_columns = source_entry["RelationalTable"]["InputColumns"]
        source_type = "RelationalTable"
    elif "S3Source" in source_entry:
        input_columns = source_entry["S3Source"]["InputColumns"]
        source_type = "S3Source"
    elif "CustomSql" in source_entry:
        input_columns = source_entry["CustomSql"]["Columns"]
        source_type = "CustomSql"
    else:
        raise ValueError(f"Unknown physical table type: {list(source_entry.keys())}")
    print(f"      Source type: {source_type}")
    print(f"      Input columns: {len(input_columns)}")
    col_id_map = {col["Name"]: col.get("Id", col["Name"]) for col in input_columns}
    # --- 1. Map column descriptions and synonyms ---
    print("\n[3/5] Building enrichment...")
    column_metadata = []
    for tc in topic["Columns"]:
        col_id = col_id_map.get(tc["ColumnName"])
        if not col_id:
            continue
        column_metadata.append({
            "ColumnNames": [tc["ColumnName"]],
            "ColumnProperties": [{
                "Description": {"Text": tc.get("ColumnDescription", "")},
                "AdditionalNotes": {"Text": ("The synonym for the column is " + ", ".join(tc.get("ColumnSynonyms", []))) if tc.get("ColumnSynonyms") else ""}
            }]
        })
    # --- 2. Add calculated fields ---
    if uses_new_experience:
        dest_key = list(data_prep["DestinationTableMap"].keys())[0]
        last_step = data_prep["DestinationTableMap"][dest_key]["Source"]["TransformOperationId"]
        for step_id, step in data_prep["TransformStepMap"].items():
            if "CastColumnTypesStep" in step:
                for op in step["CastColumnTypesStep"].get("CastColumnTypeOperations", []):
                    op.pop("SubType", None)
        for i, calc in enumerate(topic.get("CalculatedFields", [])):
            col_name = calc["CalculatedFieldName"].upper().replace(" ", "_")
            col_id = f"col-{col_name.lower().replace('_', '-')}"
            step_id = f"topic-calc-step-{i}"
            data_prep["TransformStepMap"][step_id] = {
                "CreateColumnsStep": {
                    "Alias": f"Add {calc['CalculatedFieldName']}",
                    "Columns": [{"ColumnName": col_name, "ColumnId": col_id, "Expression": calc["Expression"]}],
                    "Source": {"TransformOperationId": last_step}
                }
            }
            last_step = step_id
            column_metadata.append({
                "ColumnNames": [col_name],
                "ColumnProperties": [{
                    "Description": {"Text": calc.get("CalculatedFieldDescription", "")},
                    "AdditionalNotes": {"Text": ("The synonym for the column is " + ", ".join(calc.get("CalculatedFieldSynonyms", []))) if calc.get("CalculatedFieldSynonyms") else ""}
                }]
            })
        data_prep["DestinationTableMap"][dest_key]["Source"]["TransformOperationId"] = last_step
    else:
        lt_key = list(logical_table_map.keys())[0]
        lt = logical_table_map[lt_key]
        if "DataTransforms" in lt:
            for transform in lt["DataTransforms"]:
                if "CastColumnTypeOperation" in transform:
                    transform["CastColumnTypeOperation"].pop("SubType", None)
        for i, calc in enumerate(topic.get("CalculatedFields", [])):
            col_name = calc["CalculatedFieldName"].upper().replace(" ", "_")
            col_id = f"col-{col_name.lower().replace('_', '-')}"
            create_op = {"CreateColumnsOperation": {"Columns": [{"ColumnName": col_name, "ColumnId": col_id, "Expression": calc["Expression"]}]}}
            insert_idx = len(lt.get("DataTransforms", []))
            for idx, t in enumerate(lt.get("DataTransforms", [])):
                if "ProjectOperation" in t:
                    insert_idx = idx
                    break
            lt.setdefault("DataTransforms", []).insert(insert_idx, create_op)
            for t in lt.get("DataTransforms", []):
                if "ProjectOperation" in t:
                    t["ProjectOperation"]["ProjectedColumns"].append(col_name)
                    break
            column_metadata.append({
                "ColumnNames": [col_name],
                "ColumnProperties": [{
                    "Description": {"Text": calc.get("CalculatedFieldDescription", "")},
                    "AdditionalNotes": {"Text": ("The synonym for the column is " + ", ".join(calc.get("CalculatedFieldSynonyms", []))) if calc.get("CalculatedFieldSynonyms") else ""}
                }]
            })
    # --- 3. Build CustomInstructions text ---
    lines = []
    if custom_instructions_str:
        lines.append(custom_instructions_str)
    for entity in topic.get("NamedEntities", []):
        synonyms = ", ".join(entity.get("EntitySynonyms", []))
        fields = ", ".join(d.get("FieldName", "") for d in entity.get("Definition", []))
        entry = f"Entity {entity['EntityName']}: {entity.get('EntityDescription', '')}"
        if fields:
            entry += f" (fields: {fields})"
        if synonyms:
            entry += f" (synonyms: {synonyms})"
        lines.append(entry)
    for f in topic.get("Filters", []):
        fname = f.get("FilterName", "Unnamed")
        field = f.get("OperandFieldName", "")
        ftype = f.get("FilterType", "")
        if ftype == "CATEGORY_FILTER":
            cf = f.get("CategoryFilter", {})
            func = cf.get("CategoryFilterFunction", "")
            values = cf.get("Constant", {}).get("CollectiveConstant", {}).get("ValueList", [])
            inverse = cf.get("Inverse", False)
            op = "NOT IN" if inverse else "IN"
            lines.append(f"Business Rule - {fname}: Filter where {field} {func} {op} [{', '.join(values)}].")
        elif ftype == "NUMERIC_RANGE_FILTER":
            nrf = f.get("NumericRangeFilter", {})
            agg = nrf.get("Aggregation", "")
            inclusive = nrf.get("Inclusive", False)
            minimum = nrf.get("Constant", {}).get("RangeConstant", {}).get("Minimum", "")
            maximum = nrf.get("Constant", {}).get("RangeConstant", {}).get("Maximum", "")
            if minimum:
                op2 = "&amp;gt;=" if inclusive else "&amp;gt;"
                lines.append(f"Business Rule - {fname}: Filter where {agg}({field}) {op2} {minimum}.")
            elif maximum:
                op2 = "&amp;lt;=" if inclusive else "&amp;lt;"
                lines.append(f"Business Rule - {fname}: Filter where {agg}({field}) {op2} {maximum}.")
    instruction_text = "\n".join(lines)
    # --- 4. Assemble SemanticModelConfiguration ---
    topic_desc = topic_raw["Topic"].get("Description", "")
    if uses_new_experience:
        dest_key = list(data_prep["DestinationTableMap"].keys())[0]
    else:
        dest_key = lt_key
    semantic_model_config = {
        "TableMap": {
            "semantic-table": {
                "Alias": "Semantic Table",
                "DestinationTableId": dest_key,
                "SemanticMetadata": {"ColumnMetadata": column_metadata}
            }
        },
    }
    if topic_desc or instruction_text:
        semantic_entry = {}
        if topic_desc:
            semantic_entry["Description"] = {"Text": topic_desc}
        if instruction_text:
            semantic_entry["CustomInstructions"] = [{"InlineCustomInstruction": {"InstructionText": instruction_text}}]
        semantic_model_config["SemanticMetadata"] = [semantic_entry]
    # --- Print enrichment summary ---
    print(f"      Columns enriched: {len(column_metadata)}")
    print(f"      Calculated fields added: {len(topic.get('CalculatedFields', []))}")
    print(f"      Named entities: {len(topic.get('NamedEntities', []))}")
    print(f"      Filters as rules: {len(topic.get('Filters', []))}")
    print(f"      Custom instructions: {len(instruction_text)} chars")
    # --- 5. Build and apply update payload ---
    update_payload = {
        "Name": ds["Name"],
        "PhysicalTableMap": physical_table_map,
        "ImportMode": import_mode,
        "SemanticModelConfiguration": semantic_model_config
    }
    if uses_new_experience:
        update_payload["DataPrepConfiguration"] = data_prep
    else:
        update_payload["LogicalTableMap"] = logical_table_map
    print("\n[4/5] Applying update via SigV4 API call...")
    update_response = raw_update_data_set(aws_account_id, dataset_id, update_payload, aws_region)
    print(f"\n[5/5] SUCCESS!")
    print(f"      Dataset '{ds['Name']}' enriched with Topic metadata.")
    print(f"      Status: {update_response.get('Status', 'OK')}")
    print(f"      Ingestion: {update_response.get('IngestionId', 'N/A')}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    if len(sys.argv) &amp;lt; 5:
        print(__doc__)
        sys.exit(1)
    topic_id = sys.argv[1]
    dataset_id = sys.argv[2]
    aws_account_id = sys.argv[3]
    aws_region = sys.argv[4]
    try:
        enrich_dataset(topic_id, dataset_id, aws_account_id, aws_region)
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"\n ERROR: {e}")
        sys.exit(1)&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt; 
&lt;/div&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="run-the-script"&gt;3.2 Run the script&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;Execute the script, passing your four parameters (Topic ID, Dataset ID, Account ID, and Region):&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;div class="hide-language"&gt; 
 &lt;pre&gt;&lt;code class="language-bash"&gt;python enrich_dataset.py &amp;lt;topic_id&amp;gt; &amp;lt;dataset_id&amp;gt; &amp;lt;aws_account_id&amp;gt; &amp;lt;aws_region&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt; 
&lt;/div&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="expected-output"&gt;3.3 Expected output&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;After the script completes, confirm that the enrichment was applied correctly by inspecting the dataset through the Quick Sight API or in the Quick Sight console:&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/f1f836cb4ea6efb2a0b1b99f41ad8b103eff4b59/2026/07/06/ML-21217-5.jpg" alt="Enriched dataset semantic metadata shown in the console after the script runs" width="800"&gt;&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="verify-the-output-file"&gt;3.4 Verify the output file&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;div class="hide-language"&gt; 
 &lt;pre&gt;&lt;code class="language-bash"&gt;# Check the three sections exist:
python -c "import json; d=json.load(open('enriched-payload.json')); print(list(d.keys()))"
# Expected: ['physical_table_map', 'data_prep_configuration', 'semantic_model_configuration']&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt; 
&lt;/div&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;code&gt;physical_table_map&lt;/code&gt;: unchanged from the source dataset.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;code&gt;data_prep_configuration&lt;/code&gt;: with an added &lt;code&gt;CreateColumnsStep&lt;/code&gt; for calculated fields.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;code&gt;semantic_model_configuration&lt;/code&gt;: with column descriptions, synonyms, and custom instructions (formulas, entities, and business rules).&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="validation-best-practices"&gt;Validation best practices&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;Across all scenarios, we recommend the following validation approach:&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Build a validation question set.&lt;/strong&gt; Before migration, document 10–20 natural language questions that work correctly against your current legacy Topic. These become your regression test suite.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Run side-by-side comparisons.&lt;/strong&gt; Ask the same questions against the legacy Topic (before removal) and against the enriched dataset. Results should match.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Test edge cases.&lt;/strong&gt; Try ambiguous questions, synonym variations, and multi-step queries. The enriched dataset should handle these as effectively as (or better than) the legacy Topic did.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Validate with actual users.&lt;/strong&gt; Have 2–3 business users test the enriched dataset chat experience before you retire the legacy Topic. Their natural phrasing may reveal gaps in your synonym or entity coverage.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Document behavioral differences.&lt;/strong&gt; Some behaviors will differ between legacy Topic-based querying and dataset enrichment querying: 
  &lt;ul&gt; 
   &lt;li&gt;Legacy Topic filters are pre-defined and selectable; business rules in custom instructions require the user to reference them by name or intent.&lt;/li&gt; 
   &lt;li&gt;Legacy Topic calculated fields support aggregation-level expressions; dataset calculated fields operate row-by-row (aggregations happen at query time).&lt;/li&gt; 
   &lt;li&gt;Named entities in legacy Topics have structured metadata; in dataset enrichment they’re text-based instructions.&lt;/li&gt; 
  &lt;/ul&gt; &lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="key-considerations"&gt;Key considerations&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;The &lt;code&gt;update-data-set&lt;/code&gt; API requires a full replacement of all configuration on every call. Incremental updates to individual columns aren’t supported.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Named entities and filters don’t have dedicated API fields in &lt;code&gt;SemanticModelConfiguration&lt;/code&gt;. They must be expressed as text within &lt;code&gt;CustomInstructions&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Not all legacy Topic calculation expressions translate directly to dataset-level expressions. Aggregation-based calculations may need restructuring.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Currently, you can’t upgrade legacy datasets in-place. You must create a new dataset with the new data prep experience to enrich it.&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="clean-up"&gt;Clean up&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;To avoid incurring ongoing charges, delete the AWS resources (IAM roles, Quick Sight data sources, policies) that you created as part of experimentation. For instructions, see the &lt;a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/quick/latest/userguide/what-is.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Amazon Quick documentation&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="conclusion"&gt;Conclusion&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;Dataset Enrichment in Amazon Quick moves business intelligence metadata from a separate legacy Topic layer into the dataset itself. One asset carries its own business meaning: column descriptions, synonyms, calculation logic, entity definitions, and business rules, all governed in one place.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;To get started, identify your highest-value dataset, apply enrichment using the patterns in this post, and test it in Amazon Quick chat. For the full &lt;code&gt;SemanticModelConfiguration&lt;/code&gt; API reference, see the Amazon Quick documentation. For questions and community discussion, visit the &lt;a href="https://community.amazonquicksight.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Amazon Quick Community.&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

			</item>
		<item>
		<title>Data modeling best practices for Amazon Quick Sight multi-dataset relationships</title>
		<link>https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/machine-learning/data-modeling-best-practices-for-amazon-quick-sight-multi-dataset-relationships/</link>
		
		<dc:creator><![CDATA[Ying Wang]]></dc:creator>
		<pubDate>Tue, 07 Jul 2026 17:07:49 +0000</pubDate>
				<category><![CDATA[Amazon Quick Sight]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[Amazon Quick Suite]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[Best Practices]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[Expert (400)]]></category>
		<guid isPermaLink="false">d879d15113bd3dfbac581c534668d78a570620c1</guid>

					<description>Today, we are excited to announce Multi-Dataset Relationships in Amazon Quick Sight. This new capability lets you define logical relationships between Quick Sight datasets and perform runtime joins at query time. Instead of flattening tables ahead of time, you keep each table as its own Quick Sight dataset and declare how those datasets relate to one another inside a Quick Sight Topic.</description>
										<content:encoded>&lt;p&gt;Business intelligence analysts routinely face the same challenge at the start of every analytics project: the data needed to answer a single business question lives across multiple tables. Sales transactions sit in one place, customer demographics and product attributes in another, while returns, forecasts, and operational metrics occupy still others.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;Until now, combining these tables in Amazon Quick Sight required pre-joining everything into wide, denormalized datasets before any analysis could begin. That approach works. But it forces data-modeling decisions up front, duplicates measures across different grains, introduces maintenance overhead, and typically produces a different dataset for almost every reporting scenario.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Today, we are excited to announce &lt;a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/machine-learning/build-a-unified-semantic-layer-across-datasets-with-multi-dataset-topics-in-amazon-quick/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Multi-Dataset Relationships in Amazon Quick Sight&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;. This new capability lets you define logical relationships between Quick Sight datasets and perform runtime joins at query time. Instead of flattening tables ahead of time, you keep each table as its own Quick Sight dataset and declare how those datasets relate to one another inside a Quick Sight Topic. Quick Sight then assembles precisely the join it needs for visuals, calculated fields, filters, or natural-language Q&amp;amp;A.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;This paradigm shift brings several key advantages:&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Less upfront data preparation —&lt;/strong&gt; Define relationships once. Quick Sight joins only the relevant tables at analysis time.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Preserved native granularity —&lt;/strong&gt; Each dataset maintains its own level of detail, avoiding measure duplication across grains.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Reuse across analyses —&lt;/strong&gt; A single Topic with defined relationships serves multiple analytical use cases without rebuilding datasets.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Simplified governance —&lt;/strong&gt; Manage permissions, transformations, and business logic at the individual dataset level.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Independent refresh schedules —&lt;/strong&gt; Ingest data per table at different cadences (hourly, daily, monthly) based on data volatility.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Row-level security at runtime —&lt;/strong&gt; Row-level security (RLS) rules are enforced during runtime joins, so data-access policies apply consistently across datasets.&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;In this post, we cover data modeling concepts, supported patterns, and best practices for designing your multi-dataset data model in Quick Sight. For a deep dive into each schema pattern with SQL examples and advanced workarounds, see the second post in this series, &lt;a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/machine-learning/data-modeling-patterns-for-amazon-quick-sight-multi-dataset-relationships/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Data modeling patterns for Amazon Quick Sight multi-dataset relationships&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;h2 id="why-a-runtime-relationship-based-model"&gt;Why a runtime, relationship-based model&lt;/h2&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;The traditional single-dataset model has three recurring costs:&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Upfront preparation:&lt;/strong&gt; You must decide the join shape before you know every question, often pushing logic into custom SQL or database views.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Measure duplication:&lt;/strong&gt; When you join a fact table to a higher-grain dimension, measures on the “one” side get replicated across the “many” side, inflating sums unless you carefully de-duplicate.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Dataset sprawl:&lt;/strong&gt; Each analytical scenario tends to spawn its own purpose-built flat dataset, multiplying maintenance.&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;A relationship-based model addresses all three. You model the tables once, keep each at its native level of detail, and let the engine bring in only the tables a given visual actually needs.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;h2 id="understanding-the-architecture"&gt;Understanding the architecture&lt;/h2&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;Multi-dataset relationships rely on two distinct modeling layers. Understanding how they differ helps you decide where each piece of logic belongs.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="two-layers-logical-and-physical"&gt;Two layers: Logical and physical&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Physical layer — inside a dataset.&lt;/strong&gt; A single Quick Sight dataset is where you merge physical tables together with joins, unions, SQL, and transforms into one flattened result. Think of this as combining tables that share the same grain and always belong together.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Logical layer — across datasets in a Topic.&lt;/strong&gt; Each dataset behaves as one logical table. Inside a Topic you relate these logical tables to one another. They are not merged; they stay distinct and keep their own grain. Quick Sight only combines them when a visual, calculation, filter, or chat question requires fields from more than one.&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;table border="1px" width="100%" cellpadding="10px"&gt; 
 &lt;tbody&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Concept&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Quick Sight Implementation&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Logical Table&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;A Quick Sight Dataset (can contain internal joins, transforms, calculated fields)&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Relationship&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Defined in a Quick Sight Topic between datasets via matching key columns&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Runtime Join&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Executed at query time when a visual or calculation references fields from multiple datasets&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Data Model&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;The Quick Sight Topic — serves as the container for datasets + relationships&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
 &lt;/tbody&gt; 
&lt;/table&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="how-it-works"&gt;How it works&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;ol type="1"&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Create individual datasets. Each dataset represents a logical entity, such as Sales Facts, Customer Dimension, or Product Dimension.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Create a Topic. The Topic acts as your semantic, logical data model container.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Define relationships. Specify which columns link datasets together.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Analyze. In analysis sheets, drag fields from multiple datasets, and Quick Sight performs runtime inner joins.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Chat (Q&amp;amp;A). Ask natural language questions that span datasets, and Quick Sight uses relationships to generate cross-dataset queries.&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ol&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Current release note:&lt;/strong&gt; In the current release, relationships use inner join semantics. Rows must have matching keys in both datasets to appear in results.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;h2 id="data-modeling-concepts"&gt;Data modeling concepts&lt;/h2&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;Before you design relationships, it helps to review the core building blocks of dimensional modeling.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="dimensional-modeling"&gt;Dimensional modeling&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Fact tables —&lt;/strong&gt; Contain quantitative, measurable data (revenue, quantity, cost) at a specific grain. Fact tables are typically narrow and tall.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Dimension tables —&lt;/strong&gt; Contain descriptive attributes (customer name, product category, store location) that provide context. Dimension tables are typically wide and short.&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;table border="1px" width="100%" cellpadding="10px"&gt; 
 &lt;tbody&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Schema&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Description&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;When to Use&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Star Schema&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Single fact table surrounded by dimension tables, all directly connected&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Simple, fast queries; recommended default&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Snowflake Schema&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Star schema with normalized (decomposed) dimension tables&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Reducing redundancy in large dimensions&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Galaxy / Constellation&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Multiple fact tables sharing conformed dimensions&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Cross-process analytics (Sales vs.&amp;nbsp;Returns)&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
 &lt;/tbody&gt; 
&lt;/table&gt; 
&lt;div style="width: 810px" class="wp-caption alignnone"&gt;
 &lt;img loading="lazy" src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/f1f836cb4ea6efb2a0b1b99f41ad8b103eff4b59/2026/06/29/ML-21287-1.png" alt="Star, snowflake, and galaxy/constellation schema patterns showing fact and dimension table arrangements" width="800" height="1278"&gt;
 &lt;p class="wp-caption-text"&gt;Star, Snowflake, and Galaxy/Constellation schema patterns&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/div&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="hierarchy-types-in-dimensions"&gt;Hierarchy types in dimensions&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;table border="1px" width="100%" cellpadding="10px"&gt; 
 &lt;tbody&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Hierarchy Type&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Description&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Example&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Balanced (Fixed-depth)&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Every branch has the same number of levels&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Year &amp;gt; Quarter &amp;gt; Month &amp;gt; Day&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Ragged (Variable-depth)&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Branches have different depths; some levels skipped&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Country &amp;gt; State &amp;gt; City (some have no State)&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Recursive (Self-ref)&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Table references itself via parent-child keys&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Employee &amp;gt; Manager (org chart)&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Split (Parallel)&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Entity belongs to multiple independent hierarchies&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Product has Brand and Category hierarchies&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
 &lt;/tbody&gt; 
&lt;/table&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/f1f836cb4ea6efb2a0b1b99f41ad8b103eff4b59/2026/06/29/ML-21287-2.png" alt="Balanced hierarchy diagram: Year to Quarter to Month to Day, every branch the same depth" width="800"&gt;&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/f1f836cb4ea6efb2a0b1b99f41ad8b103eff4b59/2026/06/29/ML-21287-3.png" alt="Ragged hierarchy diagram: Country to State to City where some branches skip the State level" width="800"&gt;&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/f1f836cb4ea6efb2a0b1b99f41ad8b103eff4b59/2026/06/29/ML-21287-4.png" alt="Recursive hierarchy diagram: Employee-to-Manager parent-child structure referencing itself" width="800"&gt;&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/f1f836cb4ea6efb2a0b1b99f41ad8b103eff4b59/2026/06/29/ML-21287-5.png" alt="Split hierarchy diagram: a Product belonging to separate Brand and Category hierarchies" width="800"&gt;&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;div style="width: 810px" class="wp-caption alignnone"&gt;
 &lt;img loading="lazy" src="https://d2908q01vomqb2.cloudfront.net/f1f836cb4ea6efb2a0b1b99f41ad8b103eff4b59/2026/06/29/ML-21287-6.png" alt="Side-by-side comparison of balanced, ragged, recursive, and split dimension hierarchy types" width="800" height="46"&gt;
 &lt;p class="wp-caption-text"&gt;Balanced, Ragged, Recursive, and Split hierarchy type diagrams&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/div&gt; 
&lt;h2 id="best-practices"&gt;Best practices&lt;/h2&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;The following practices help you build a multi-dataset model that stays performant and maintainable as it grows.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="start-with-a-star-schema"&gt;1. Start with a star schema&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;The star schema is the recommended foundation: a central fact table as the hub dataset with dimension tables radiating outward. Star schemas minimize join complexity and maximize query performance.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="design-datasets-as-logical-tables"&gt;2. Design datasets as logical tables&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;One dataset = one business concept (Customers, Products, Orders).&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Pre-join snowflake chains into a single dimension dataset when feasible.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Include surrogate keys for clean joins.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Enrich with descriptions, synonyms, and semantic types.&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="define-clean-join-keys"&gt;3. Define clean join keys&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Use integer surrogate keys where possible (faster joins, smaller storage).&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Confirm matching data types on both sides of the relationship.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Remove null values from join key columns (nulls never match in inner joins).&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Validate referential integrity. Every foreign key in the fact table should exist in the dimension.&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="manage-granularity-deliberately"&gt;4. Manage granularity deliberately&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;All datasets related to the same fact should be joinable at a compatible grain.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;If a dimension is at a coarser grain, aggregate the fact to match.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;For multi-fact models, make sure shared dimensions have a single, consistent grain.&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="enrich-metadata-for-ai-and-natural-language-accuracy"&gt;5. Enrich metadata for AI and natural language accuracy&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;Multi-Dataset Topics power Quick Sight’s natural language interface. Rich metadata dramatically improves accuracy:&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Add field descriptions explaining business meaning.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Add synonyms (such as Revenue → Sales, Income, Total Amount).&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Set semantic types (City, Currency, Date, and so on).&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Add custom instructions for business rules.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Exclude internal/technical columns users don’t need.&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="handle-multi-fact-scenarios-carefully"&gt;6. Handle multi-fact scenarios carefully&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Confirm shared dimensions have a conformed grain across all facts.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Be explicit about which relationships exist, and avoid creating unnecessary connections.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Test cross-fact calculations to verify correct aggregation.&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;h3 id="plan-for-growth"&gt;7. Plan for growth&lt;/h3&gt; 
&lt;ul&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Start with a focused model (1 fact + key dimensions). Add datasets gradually.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Document your data model by keeping a diagram of datasets and relationships.&lt;/li&gt; 
 &lt;li&gt;Use naming conventions: &lt;code&gt;FACT_*&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;DIM_*&lt;/code&gt;, &lt;code&gt;BRIDGE_*&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/li&gt; 
&lt;/ul&gt; 
&lt;h2 id="decision-framework-when-to-use-multi-dataset-vs.-pre-joined"&gt;Decision framework: When to use multi-dataset vs.&amp;nbsp;pre-joined&lt;/h2&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;The preceding best practices provide a general framework for designing robust multi-dataset models. However, not every analytics scenario calls for multi-dataset relationships. The following decision framework helps you determine when to use runtime relationships versus the traditional pre-joined dataset approach.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;table border="1px" width="100%" cellpadding="10px"&gt; 
 &lt;tbody&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Scenario&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Recommended Approach&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Simple analysis with &amp;lt; 5 tables and only 1 fact table&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Single pre-joined dataset (traditional)&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Multiple analysts asking different questions on different fact tables&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Multi-Dataset Relationships&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Need outer join behavior&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Single pre-joined dataset (or wait for future release)&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Natural language or chat-powered exploration&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Multi-Dataset Relationships with dataset and topic enrichment&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Many-to-many without a bridge table&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Multi-Dataset Relationships&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
  &lt;tr&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Role-playing dimensions&lt;/td&gt; 
   &lt;td&gt;Multi-Dataset Relationships (separate datasets per role)&lt;/td&gt; 
  &lt;/tr&gt; 
 &lt;/tbody&gt; 
&lt;/table&gt; 
&lt;h2 id="getting-started"&gt;Getting started&lt;/h2&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;To get started read &lt;a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/machine-learning/build-a-unified-semantic-layer-across-datasets-with-multi-dataset-topics-in-amazon-quick/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"&gt;Build a unified semantic layer across datasets with multi-dataset Topics in Amazon Quick&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;h2 id="next-schema-patterns-and-advanced-workarounds"&gt;Next: Schema patterns and advanced workarounds&lt;/h2&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;So far, we have covered the foundational concepts of dimensional modeling, including star, snowflake, and galaxy (constellation) schemas. We also covered general best practices for designing clean join keys, managing granularity, enriching metadata, and planning for growth.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;In the second post, we shift from theory to practice. We walk through each schema pattern in detail with concrete table structures and sample SQL queries. We also show how to handle supported scenarios such as role-playing dimensions and multi-fact models with different granularity. And we explain workarounds for patterns that are not natively supported, including circular joins, recursive hierarchies, and ragged hierarchies.&lt;/p&gt; 
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/machine-learning/data-modeling-patterns-for-amazon-quick-sight-multi-dataset-relationships/"&gt;Read Part 2: Data Modeling Patterns for Amazon Quick Sight Multi-Dataset Relationships&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
